Glowacki offers new outlook on popular shows

Stephanie Lyons, Daily Vidette Staff

Issue date: 3/27/08 = Section: News
=
  • Pri= nt
  • Email=
  • Page 1 of 2 next=20 >
Media Credit: Jenna Redline / Daily = Vidette=20 Staff
Speaker Matt Glowacki talks about = diversity=20 issues during his presentation "Diversity According to South = Park=20 and Family Guy" on Wednesday night in the Bone Student = Center.=20 =

"South = Park" and=20 "Family Guy" are most likely seen as racially stereotyped programs on=20 television, but a presentation entitled, "Diversity According to South = Park and=20 Family Guy" dug deeper into the diversity issues involved in the two=20 shows.

"It uses the two TV shows, and how diversity is shown in = there,=20 and actually how diversity is taught. I think when people really look at = the=20 cartoons they don't think about diversity and how they are actually = teaching=20 about it. They think it's very, very racial, and filled with racial = profiling=20 and stereotypes," Jarrell Jackson, chair of Redbird Diversity,=20 said.

Inspirational speaker, Matt Glowacki, discussed stereotypes = and=20 issues of diversity while incorporating clips of "Family Guy" and "South = Park."=20

"[Diversity] is a process we all engage in every single day. I = think=20 diversity should be a verb because the magic of diversity happens when = you=20 interact with people you normally would never interact with, and then = you learn=20 from them," Glowacki said.

The concept of isms tied the lecture=20 together. The first ism discussed was that of lookism.

"It is=20 discrimination towards people based on the way they look, but it could = also be=20 within a person. When you look at yourself in a negative way," Glowacki = said.=20

One out of four college aged women has some sort of eating = disorder.=20 Lookism could be a factor involved in women's body issues.

"It is = the way=20 the products are marketed to us. Every product is sold to us under this = premise=20 called fear, uncertainty and doubt. They try to make us scared or make = us feel=20 uncertain like we need something in our life to make us feel better = about=20 ourselves," Glowacki said.

Ableism is discrimination towards = people=20 based on the fact that they may have a disability. The character of Joe, = from=20 "Family Guy," was used as an example because he uses a = wheelchair.

Some=20 people react differently when they are interacting with a person who has = a=20 disability. Glowacki discussed how some people will ignore someone who = is=20 disabled while others will try to over accommodate them.=20
Continued...=20

An XPath context consists of a // DOM node, a list of DOM nodes that contains this node, a number // that represents the position of the single node in the list, and a // current set of variable bindings. (See XPath spec.) // // The interface of the expression context: // // Constructor -- gets the node, its position, the node set it // belongs to, and a parent context as arguments. Yet, some expressions are required to // evaluate to particular types, and not every type can be coerced // into every other type. (See XPath spec.) // // The four types are: // // StringValue // // NumberValue // // BooleanValue // // NodeSetValue // // The common interface of the value classes consists of methods that // implement the XPath type coercion rules: // // stringValue() -- returns the value as a JavaScript String, // // numberValue() -- returns the value as a JavaScript Number, // // booleanValue() -- returns the value as a JavaScript Boolean, // // nodeSetValue() -- returns the value as a JavaScript Array of DOM // Node objects. // function StringValue(value) { this.value =3D value; this.type =3D 'string'; } StringValue.prototype.stringValue =3D function() { return this.value; } StringValue.prototype.booleanValue =3D function() { return this.value.length > 0; } StringValue.prototype.numberValue =3D function() { return this.value - 0; } StringValue.prototype.nodeSetValue =3D function() { throw this + ' ' + Error().stack; } function BooleanValue(value) { this.value =3D value; this.type =3D 'boolean'; } BooleanValue.prototype.stringValue =3D function() { return '' + this.value; } BooleanValue.prototype.booleanValue =3D function() { return this.value; } BooleanValue.prototype.numberValue =3D function() { return this.value ?
